Through traveling for television promos that are illegally hacked into Panem's network to fighting in staged events, she is the voice of the people. But missing at her side is her fellow Tribute, Peeta, who was seized by the Capitol at the same time she was rescued. He's alive - but acting strangely. What has the Capitol done to him?    In \\"Mockingjay\\", Collins brings the series to an explosive conclusion. I've seen several reviews that state the reader was disappointed in the ending, and to a certain extent, I can see why. Butin order to fully appreciate this work, you have to look at it as a novel about revolution. In actual wars, tough decisions must be made. Not everyone survives. Life isn't black-and-white and we don't get the stereotypical \\"happy ending\\". These are things that come to the front of Katniss's mind, as she must decide what to do to put the horror of her past behind her - and live for the future.

In a wise move, Lopez scratched those songs from her catalog and went to find some popular producers to help her on what would become her Love? album.  The result is a very upbeat and danceable album that has J.Lo treading new territory for her.  This in itself is good, but the result is still mindless, generic, forgettable pop music.  The album isn't totally bad, however.  Several songs will have you dancing, but you won't find anything that breaks the mold that's been firmly cast by the Britneys, Rihannas and Ke$has of the world.    First single, \\"On The Floor\\" (which heavily samples Kaoma's \\"Lambada\\"), does a fine enough job of showing off the direction of the album.  What follows from that is a collection of hit-or-miss songs.  The more impressive songs are those that feature production from RedOne and have that pop/dance sound.  \\"On The Floor\\", \\"Papi\\", \\"Invading My Mind\\", \\"Hypnotico\\" and \\"Charge Me Up\\" are the highlights of the album by far.  In particular, \\"Invading My Mind\\" and \\"Hypnotico\\" are the two stellar stand-out tracks, both of which happen to be written and/or produced by none other than Lady Gaga.  \\"Hypnotico\\" needs to be a single...this song is absolutely fantastic and is Love?'s absolute shining moment.    Other songs come close to being great.  \\"Until It Beats No More\\" benefits from some stellar production which transforms the song from a run-of-the-mill love song into a groovy number with a great beat.  Unfortunately, Lopez' voice just cannot carry this song (I can see someone like Leona Lewis making this song a classic).  J.Lo's vocal shortcomings are also evident in \\"Starting Over\\" and \\"Villain\\", which sound noisy and disheveled.  Among the album's worst moments are \\"Good Hit\\", which is an embarrassing autotune overkill number, and \\"I'm Into You\\" which has probably the most elementary writing making it sound like a broken record...plus Lil Wayne does the song no favors.    While this album is decent, overall it's not as strong as her other albums, such as This Is Me...Then, Rebirth or Brave.  I hope it does well, and with some good decisions on her label's part it could yield some big hits for Mrs. Lopez.  But really it's just your typical, generic pop album.

0761536434|3.0|Former video game reviewer Steven Kent wrote this rollicking history of the video game industry: the companies that made the games, and the people--which is to say, with very few exceptions, the men--behind the companies.<br /><br />It's a little dry at times but better overall than the sloppy and jocular [[ASIN:0307463559 All Your Base Are Belong to Us: How Fifty Years of Videogames Conquered Pop Culture]]. More than 500 interviews gave Kent tons of quotes and plenty of historical context. Again, this book is more about the people than the games themselves. You won't get much insight into gameplay and you won't get more than one or two photos of games in the entire book, period. The title may therefore seem misleading to some readers. On the plus side, there's lots of detail on legal proceedings and what transpired behind the scenes to get the games to market, or in some cases, to keep them off the shelves. If you want a history of games themselves, Kent is the first to suggest Leonard Herman's [[ASIN:0964384825 Phoenix: The Fall & Rise of Videogames]]. For a tasty visual retrospective, try my own favorite, [[ASIN:0762409371 Arcade Fever: The Fan's Guide To The Golden Age Of Video Games]].<br /><br />As for The Ultimate History of Video Games, it's a HUGE book: almost six hundred pages--with wide margins, in all fairness--in the Prima Publishing First Edition. Published in 2001, this will obviously not reflect the last ten years of gaming. Still, the meat of Kent's many interviews with notable personalities from the industry's formative years is informative and entertaining.

B000055X3U|5.0|Following the austere minimalism of the dejected Alternative 4, Anathema return to the elaborate instrumental style and vast compositional scope of Eternity on their fifth album, Judgement, an album characterized by diverse expansions of traditional rock-song formats, arranged with the compositional insight for melodic development and atmospheric layering, expressed with a more hopeful spirit than previous works, but with the band's trademark fluidity in merging of rhythm and tone toward thematic representation, orchestrated for maximum emotional impact. After an album scarce in instrumental expressiveness, listeners are graced with the sound of Danny Cavanagh's dynamically communicative guitar-playing, his performance here ranking as his most spirited and potently expressive, Judgement abundant with moments of pure sonic bliss in the form of Cavanagh's lead playing, highlights of which are the blistering solo in the charged \\"Pitiless\\", his tender atmospheric touches in the serene \\"2000 & Gone\\", the soulful quality of his subtle melodies during the intro and outro of \\"Emotional Winter\\", the heart-wrenching overflow of sorrowful emotion that is the solo of the grieving \\"One Last Goodbye\\", and the soaring tranquility of his playing during the fantastic coda of \\"Wings Of God\\"; the guitar-work of the Cavanagh brothers on this release is phenomenal, capturing a wide range of feelings in both electric and acoustic guitars, using the latter to great affect in delicately expressing the fragility of desperate loneliness; their skill in creating unfolding melodies continuously blossoming through transitions determining harmonic substance provides the music with a wonderful communicative essence, reflecting lyrical themes in the conceptual design of musical passages.    \\"Solitude was never seen as loneliness   And things need time   And time leads to other things   And playing roles   Which are limited   By the poor fund of knowledge   In this sick, sick world   We all fall down   Once in a while   Escaping the law of the unexplained pains\\"    The scope of songwriting is more expansive than the individually composed songs of Alternative 4, as most of the writing on Judgement is shared between the musicians, including new bassist Dave Pybus who replaces longtime bassist and songwriter Duncan Patterson, the songs here are more fleshed out and versatile, while continuing the band's characteristic contrasting movements of climactic intention, similar in method to progressive rock but not in aesthetic purpose; the expressive character of the music is highly concentrated on creating eloquent melodies of flowing atmospheric quality as opposed to ever-shifting patterns of energetically animated music in complex structures; witness the ethereal elegance of \\"Make It Right\\", the spatial immensity of \\"Emotional Winter\\", and the dramatic shifts in enveloping waves of thematic articulation in \\"Wings Of God\\" for prime examples of this band's brilliance in actualizing their versatile expressive purpose. Vincent Cavanagh has developed into an outstanding vocalist, delivering his most consistently captivating performance since taking over the role of lead singer, granting the music an impassioned force with a keen sense of melody working in perfect harmony with the guitars, complimented occasionally by heavenly female vocals, his soaring cries and the graceful quality of his melodic articulations at times accentuated by the dreamy ambience of keyboards or punctuated by a piano; since many of these songs were arranged to emphasize Vincent's increasingly compelling and emotively powerful singing, the album's atmospheric quality is dependent to a considerable extent on his performance, as is the flow of the entire album, which is sequenced much like the continuously evolving  Eternity; Anathema want to give their audience an experience in the form of an album developing its unifying themes in an active exploration from beginning to end, and Judgement  delivers this in remarkable fashion.    \\"All the hate that feeds your needs   All the sickness you conceive   All the horror you create   Will bring you to your knees\\"    Kit Woolven's production provides instrumental clarity and promotes the ambient elements of the band's sound, yet the pleasant return of original drummer John Douglas is marred somewhat by the production's lack of fullness in the low-end sound, meaning that the natural fluidity and power of Douglas's playing loses presence of sound and impact. But the texture of the instrumentation is vividly pronounced in the sound, working to the music's intention of sweeping the listener into lavish atmospheres, arousing the dream of freedom...freedom from the illusions and limitations of a transient existence, suspended in the fantasy of a beautiful escape, until you come back down to the reality of an earthly existence, but this time Anathema won't let you drown in the ocean of your despair, as they now sing songs urging you to break down your emotional force-fields and engage honestly with your emotions, come to understanding through trust, and feel life in all its temporal glory by embracing the moment of being alive, and come to terms with your mistakes of a past kept alive only in memory, no longer a slave in the chains of the past, now free to seize the preciousness of the present moment and bask in the beautiful tragedy of this life. This is the hopeful message of Judgement, a hopeful message that acknowledges pain and suffering as a condition of existence to be honestly confronted and embraced toward a deeper and more fulfilling connection with ourselves and the world around us; this realization and acceptance is inherent in the spiritual fabric of the music, brought to life through a near perfection in compositional application of artistic vision and the full-on immersion of the band members into the creation of their ideas in musical form, making Judgement the band's most expressively powerful work.

B004IQMXD4|5.0|\\"In Your Dreams\\", Stevie Nicks' seventh solo album and her first in ten years, has really shown how the artist has come full circle. As a whole, it is one of her strongest to date, many already comparing it to \\"Bella Donna.\\" A lengthy record of 13 tracks (14 if you count the extra track available on some editions), Miss Nicks has certainly proven herself to be prolific. Obviously the strongest element here is simply the artist's voice--which sounds stronger and more capable than ever. Miss Nicks has certainly matured in both her singing and in her songwriting. The very first listen brought tears to the eyes.    There are many gems on this album, and of course there are the obvious standouts. \\"In Your Dreams\\", \\"Annabel Lee\\", \\"You May Be The One\\", and \\"Italian Summer\\" are going to be the memorable tracks. The title track starts out sounding somewhat like a Hidden Valley commercial, but is quite catchy and in no way offensive. The touch of rockabilly makes it very suitable for radio play. \\"You May Be The One\\" is an old-style, bluesy number, the kind of song for which the artist's voice was made. Even \\"Moonlight (A Vampire's Dream)\\", a.k.a. \\"The Vampire Song\\", is quite beautiful--and this reviewer admittedly has never read or seen a single episode of Twilight.    Notably present here is a clear element of country, an element which has resurfaced in a number of her tracks throughout her long career: \\"I Don't Want To Know\\" ('Rumours'), \\"After the Glitter Fades\\" ('Bella Donna'), \\"That's Alright\\" ('Mirage'), \\"No Questions Asked\\" ('Fleetwood Mac Greatest Hits'), \\"Affairs of the Heart\\" ('Behind The Mask'), \\"Rose Garden\\" ('Street Angel')--none of which is surprising for a girl from Arizona. \\"For What It's Worth\\" could easily be played on any country station; the chorus of \\"New Orleans\\" could have been penned by Kenny Chesney. Even \\"Cheaper Than Free\\" reveals a hint of country, particularly in the guitar solo. Here Stevie confirms what she has always claimed, that one of her biggest influences aside from Joplin and Hendrix, is and always has been her late grandfather, AJ Nicks--with whom she first started singing as a very young girl.    The obvious gem of this record--and granted this is a strictly subjective statement--is \\"Everybody Loves You\\", co-written with Dave Stewart. It is the strongest track on the record, performed with Mr. Stewart, whose deep baritone compliments Stevie's most appropriately. The lyrics are sweet and poignant, and seem to be a reflection of the artist's life, as are many of her songs: \\"Everybody loves you, but you're so alone. Everybody knows your name, but you can't find your way home. No one really knows you; I'm the only one.\\" For me this track is simply one of her best. Ever.    On the flip side, \\"Soldier's Angel\\" is clearly the weak link of the line-up. While noble in intent, and beautifully sung, it is awkward in its presentation even with Lindsey Buckingham's backing harmonizing vocals. Reminiscent of 1991's \\"Desert Angel\\", but not nearly as strong a track, and like \\"Illume (9-11)\\" from Fleetwood Mac's 'Say You Will' album of 2003, it is clearly meant to acknowledge and provide a personal commentary on current events. At least two other tracks from the record provide similar commentaries, but do so in a much more subtle way.    Ms. Nicks tends to repeat herself in a number of ways, many of which we are used to seeing in her former work. She lifts lines from previous songs, just as she always has (\\"come in out of the darkness\\", \\"no words were spoken\\", \\"lady from the mountains\\", \\"no one walks away from this battle\\", \\"sometimes it was heavenly, sometimes it was too heavy\\", and that ever persistent \\"ghost through the fog\\"). Sometimes this self-referencing works; at other times, it can be somewhat off putting, even to her most loyal listeners.    Miss Nicks also has the tendency to repeat certain concepts or words in her songs: \\"angel\\", the aforementioned \\"ghost\\", and \\"child\\" come to mind here. Clearly she likes to use certain types of words like \\"angel\\" and \\"child\\", as she enunciates them well and they work particularly well with her voice. Angels, ghosts, and dreams have always been a common thread in most of Miss Nicks' work, with \\"dreams\\" having figured prominently in her writing since the days of 'Rumours'.    And finally, a noticeable `blooper' that occurs in one of her songs here: you can clearly hear Dave Stewart providing a musical cue, \\"Here we go\\", faintly, just after the intro to the track \\"New Orleans\\", which, I have to admit, I found more amusing than anything else. Even the best are human and can miss a thing or two in their time!    In any case, at sixty something, Miss Nicks has certainly earned her keep--and can pretty much write whatever the heck she wants.    We will still listen. And be moved appropriately.

1416594787|4.0|This isn't the best introductory book I've read on evolution, Dawkins loves to insult the people who don't hold his views, goes way to far sometimes to get his point across and has a tendency to ramble on and mention interesting but irrelevant stuff.  Once you get past the flaws this actually is a pretty good book, oddly by the end some of those qualities I hated about the book in the beginning, I started to appreciate more in the end (I kind of enjoy the almost pointless side stories and facts).      When I started reading this book, I put it down for a while because I got tired of the creationist rants, which apparently the high number of people who deny evolution is why this book is written.  Dawkins even goes as far as comparing an evolution denier as the equivalent of someone denying the existence of the roman civilization or even worse a holocaust denier.  I'm sorry but lacking the understanding or denying evolution is nothing like denying the holocaust.  For one thing we've never really witnessed one animal evolving into another completely different species, meaning one \\"kind\\" into another \\"kind\\", in our lifetime (which is far too short of a time scale) or even more a bacteria evolving into a mammal, this doesn't mean evolution is false (its not), but it is far different than denying the holocaust.  Anyways eventually I picked the book back up and it was far better as I got further into it.  Also expect to hear the word \\"history-deniers\\" every few pages, I guess he wants us to remember just how terrible the evolution deniers are.  Since this book is written to convince the 40% of American who deny evolution, Dawkins should realize by now that insulting your target audience isn't the best way to get them to listen to you.  If anything his books do more help to the young earth creationist movement and intelligent design.     The subtitle of this book is \\"The Evidence for Evolution\\", which is kind of an unfitting title, I found that Coyne's Why Evolution is Truecontains far more evidence in far fewer pages and is overall a better introduction to evolution.   You see Dawkins often goes off on rants which do not to move the evidence along. For example in a chapter he discusses the age of the earth, he spends several pages discussing getting the age from tree rings.  You see you can match the width of tree rings with others and go back to earlier dates, but then he says that the chain of tree rings goes back 11,000 years only, well the pages he spent on this argument do nothing to convince a young earth creationist of the age of the earth, in fact the argument works in their favor.  The book is full of these little side notes and stories which causes the page numbers to go up, but the relevant information doesn't follow.   Also expect tons of foot notes with mostly rants about TV shows he wants to be on, his childhood, or why we should call the Beijing Man, the Peking fossil, ect.    I know I've complained some but don't get me wrong, this book, once you look past the flaws, is still very interesting and worth reading (assuming that you're not a creationist).  Many of the side stories which I complained about are actually interesting if you don't mind frequent diversions and he goes into DNA a little more than the other non DNA specific evolution books I've read.  So in the end I do think its pretty good, just not as a first book on evolution.

1401207529|5.0|Frank Miller's take on the origins of Batman is a refreshing and well paced story from start to end.    I'm not great at reviewing in the traditional paragraph form so I've decided to do pros and cons and to keep this review as short and concise as possible.    PRO:  - The story is as simple as they come all the while still leaving a fulfilling feeling at the end of it. There was never a dull moment and I really enjoyed myself throughout the whole thing.  - The art is amazing. David Mazzucchelli brings a unique and bold art style to the world of Gotham. He uses bold strong lines with shades and contour that should be admired. I don't want to spoil it but it's great and quite possibly the best part of this piece.  - The story is half Batman and half Jim Gordon. This works out extremely well because somehow they manage to make Gordon's arrival at the Gotham PD and Wayne's transformation into Batman equally interesting. Just as you're beginning to tire of one of them, the other takes over the panels and by the end when they are sharing panels it seems like a great pay off.   - One thing I despise in comics is when the writer turns to dialogue and makes the whole thing too wordy. Frank Miller excels in showing not telling and I really wish that more comic writers would work close with their illustrator to achieve this. Never did I look at a page and feel daunted by the amount of dialogue or wordiness on the page. Comics are meant to tell a story but they are not meant to be books with a picture fighting a text bubble for attention.  - An after word by artist David Mazzucchelli is a very nice way to wrap up the book and provides a nice insight into what he was trying to achieve in illustrating year one.    CON:  - It is short. I wish there was more to read but that's just because it is so well done. It is 96 pages of pure genius and I wish it were that plus a couple zero's at the end of that number.  - There is a catwoman origin stuck in their that seemed rushed and notso great. I think given time and space it could have grown and become something substancial but it seemed cut off and no closure was brought to the character.  - The beginning is abrupt and doesn't give as much background that I would have liked but that's a small complaint in an otherwise perfect story structure.      Overall the comic is a great addition to anyone's collection and Miller should be commended for his simplistic yet deep style of telling a story. All in all, perfect Batman origins comic and a great comic for a person to get started in the character.

You can learn some techniques by reading this book, but it is NOT a how-to guide.  The book does talk a lot about how it all works, it's just not a step-by-step guide so please don't expect that. The chapter dealing Daniel Tammets was a complete surprise and almost worth the price of the book alone.  If you go into this book realizing it's a biographical narrative, with some interesting science and technique thrown in and not expecting something else, you will likely be please.  I definitely recommend it.

B004OEIL54|5.0|So many will wonder why I claim this is a forgotten classic. I mean isn't the SCREAM mask still sold at Halloween? Haven't we just seen a new sequel released? Isn't the movie spoken of in every Wes Craven interview?<br /><br />All of these things might be true but the fact remains that while SCREAM did do big box office, was sequelized and is talked about at times, I found in watching it again that it was a much better film than I recalled. It was scarier than I remembered. It was better made than I thought at first. And it works on so many levels as to be considered a classic.<br /><br />For those uninitiated the film tells the story of a group of teenage friends. The film opens with Casey (Drew Barrymore) receiving an anonymous phone call with someone who at first flirts with her and then threatens her. In short order she not only witnesses her boyfriend's demise but is soon murdered herself by a killer in a stretched ghost face mask and flowing black tattered robe.<br /><br />The next day the kids at her high school are upset when they hear of the murders. But as teens go they also tend to move on to the next thing that interests them, a true example of A.D.D. Enter our main character Sidney (Neve Campbell), a young woman whose boyfriend Billy (Skeet Ulrich) wants to take things to another level but who remains chaste. Her best friend Tatum (Rose McGowan) isn't quite as pure. Tatum's boyfriend Stuart (Matthew Lillard) is the court jester, making jokes at all times. Rounding out this group is Randy (Jamie Kennedy) the nerd of pack who works at the local video store and is a movie fanatic.<br /><br />As the film progresses so does the body count. With each murder we also get a glimpse of the killer and the fact that he seems to be a bit of a bumbler compared to the villains other slasher films have delivered in the past. Where the cool killer reigned in most, this killer trips over his costume, gets knocked in the head more than once and gets downed occasionally only to mysteriously disappear. While choosing to wear a goofy mask this seems like more of what a real serial killer might be like, a klutz who makes mistakes.<br /><br />The cast is rounded out by David Arquette as Deputy Dewey, Tatum's brother and the local goofball policeman. Dewey comes off as little more than a Don Knotts/Barney Fife knock off. But beneath it all lies something more than gets revealed a piece at a time in all of the SCREAM movies.<br /><br />Offsetting this character is Gale Weathers (Courtney Cox), a driven newswoman who will do anything to get the story and advance her career. At the moment she is not well liked by Sidney whose life story Gale has pitched on more than one occasion. Sidney's mother was murdered earlier and Sidney has identified Cotton Weary (Liev Schrieber) as the killer. Gale has taken Cotton's side in the matter and has done all she can to get his release much to the displeasure of Sidney.<br /><br />Now the nice part about all of these characters is that each one has a reason to be the killer and the opportunity over and over again. We constantly wonder who the killer is and each time you think you know you find yourself pausing to consider the next person. Is Dewey really hiding his homicidal tendencies behind the goofy faade? Is Gale so determined to get Cotton released that she'd do anything to see it happen? Could Billy have had a reason to become the killer since his mother left him? Every character bops in and out of the scene with ample opportunity to jump back in as the killer.<br /><br />At the heart of this is Randy, the movie nerd, who takes the time at a party to discuss the ins and outs of horror films and \\"the rules\\". So many actually fit any number of films that have been released its hilarious. For instance the rule that if you're a virgin you're safe. Having sex always results in being the next victim. Or never say \\"I'll be right back\\" when leaving a room since it usually results in your chances of returning being non-existent.<br /><br />What makes this movie so good is that it keeps your guessing like the best whodunit ever made. You find yourself thinking it's this person then another then another until you're never quite sure who you think did it. And then result, the reveal, was a tremendous surprise when this film was first released. Even knowing who the killer is doesn't spoil the fun watching it again as you catch the clues left throughout.<br /><br />The movie is also fun because of the in jokes that many movie fans will catch. Names of characters, locations, little aside dropped in all make the movie hilarious with each one. The best one is when high school principal Henry Winkler hears a noise in the hall, sticks his head out and sees the school janitor (played by director Wes Craven) wearing a green and red striped long sleeved sweater who grunts at him, to which Winkler replies \\"Sorry, Fred\\". Yes, a direct reference to Craven's best known film A NIGHTMARE ON ELM STREET.<br /><br />The SCREAM films are being released in blu-ray format for the first time from Lionsgate who recently picked up the distribution rights. They've done a great job with it, just in time for the release of the latest sequel. Best of all its nice to see the film come out in a clean format that means it can be appreciated again for some and for the first time for others. Believe it or not the movie IS fifteen years old now. So if you're watching it with someone who hasn't seen it don't let them know who the killer is, sit back and watch them try to figure it out and enjoy the ride.at it keeps your guessing like the best whodunit ever made. B003VANOFY|5.0|I bought this headset at Best Buy last month to replace my wireless stereo headphones from Creative.  Set up on Windows 7 64-bit was easy. You can auto-mux all your sounds to the headphone, or if you have multiple speakers, mux your ventrilio to your outside source, game to your headphones, etc.  G930 software is a bit basic, leaving you to decide how to advance calibrate presets for games.  The voice morphing software was a nice novelty to mess around with, but ultimately unecessary bloat.  I would have preferred better EQ presets.    I tried these headphones on World of Warcraft, Call of Duty Black Ops, and Battlefield Bad Company 2 for PC.  Easily the best sound out of the three is Battlefield.  The game had several different settings to try out, War Tapes being my favorite as it adds reverberation algorythm and extra bass for explosions.  You could actually hear the rustling of people's clothing while walking around in cut scenes.  Pretty amazing to hear the care their sound engineers put into the game.      However, the reason why most people using gaming headphones are to hear the sound indicators.  For example, there are distinct sounds to hear in shooters like footsteps, or spell abilities being used like in Warcraft.  After fooling with the sound settings in the G930 software, I found bass/ sub capabilities were only apparent in the side (stereo) speakers.  When isolating the front and back portions of the surround sound, they were very tin-can sounding; even with the subwoofer option turned up.  It was apparent emphasis was placed on the stereo portion of gameplay, with little regard for establishing a good center-channel speaker.  When playing shooters, it was hard to distinguish front and back sounds, such as a person walking behind me versus the front.  There is also a slight sound delay from control inputs to actual sound production.  It wasn't enough to be noticable, but running sound through different sources indicated a slight delay in the headphones. After taking the black foam covering the speakers off, it was painfully obvious many of the issues with sound distinction came from the placement of the speakers inside of the headphone.  It appears some of the channels are simulated surround sound, not actual.  It goes to show, headphones are still no substitute to having a good traditional 5.1 surround set up.     Still though the sound isolation, ease of use, wireless characteristics, and bass quality far outweight the G930 drawbacks.  The headphones come with a stereo-surround switch to adjust to stereo programs such as Ventrilio, Winamp and Youtube videos on-the-fly.  The volume knob is conveniently located next to the stereo-surround switch button, making adjustments a snap.  I still haven't found a use for the G-keys, though it is a nice novelty for those who need them.      Provided you have a good sound card, you can source your PS3 / XBOX 360 sound through your computer (via optical in/out), letting you use these headphones for the systems. It can be a real money saver for those who are worried these can only be used via PC.  I've enjoyed these headphones thoroughly for casual gaming, and recommend these for anyone needing a better edge with game sound indicators without the standard 5.1 setup.
B003UESJH4|5.0|There are many times when the film picked for best picture at the Oscars tend to be what many would consider the wrong film. Too often these days the award is given to a prestige picture, a film that no one saw and chances are that they won't even though it won the award. Popular pictures seem to be ignored for more artistic films. This past year saw a marriage of the two, a film that not only entertained and did decent at the box office but that told a solid tale without resorting to simplistic feats. That film arrives on DVD this week, THE KING'S SPEECH.<br /><br />Opening in 1925, the Duke of York, Albert Frederick Arthur George, was the younger of two brothers to King George V. Played here with a combination of weakness and strength by Colin Firth (who won the Oscar for best actor); Albert is a beaten man when it comes to all things royal. He knows his brother is heir to the crown and is fine with that. But he's had a problem since childhood that affects him on a daily basis. He is quite tongue tied with a stammer that impedes him from making any speeches whatsoever.<br /><br />Consulting doctor after doctor with the help of his wife Elizabeth (Helena Bonham Carter) he all but gives up hope. Then she hears of a doctor of a different sort, one who has a record of being able to help each patient sent his way.<br /><br />Lionel Logue (Geoffrey Rush) is unconventional at best. An Australian now in London, he takes on case after case while hoping to land a career in the theatre. With the arrival of Elizabeth and sworn to secrecy, he sets the ground rules. It is he who will decided if he takes the case or not and when in his locale both men become equals. To make his point, he takes to calling Albert \\"Bertie\\", a nickname only members of the royal family have used in the past. While Albert isn't aware, Lionel understands it's not the symptoms that just need treated but the cause as well. And until Albert comes to grips with this, the cure will only be temporary.<br /><br />The two men work on a daily basis as Lionel helps Albert overcome his fears to a certain extent. He does improve but near as much as he would like. With the help of Logue, he makes it through the ceremony and is now King George VI. But fires are burning across Europe. Hitler is on the move and soon makes his play in Poland. And now Bertie must gather together his strength and inspire a nation with a speech. Has all the work paid off or not?<br /><br />Based on the true history of these two men, the film slowly develops not just the story but shows the development of the two men as well. One born into high society and the other the son of a drunk, they have little in common and yet learn more from one another than would be expected. And through their learning they become possibly the best friend that either of them has ever had.<br /><br />Not only did the film win for best picture it also garnered Oscars for best screenplay and best director. Most definitely. This is a story that inspires just with the tale alone. There are no outward heroics with guns blazing. Instead we are inspired by the courage of one man to face his fears, to overcome his disability and to become the voice of his nation.<br /><br />The true test to me of a good film is if I would consider watching it again. B0015I2P0Y|4.0|I sometimes wonder whether I emphasize my like of difference in music over quality and musicality.  I tend to rate music from artists that create unusual music higher than mainstream artists.  Elbow creates gorgeous and mellow music that is close to the mainstream, but far enough away from the mainstream to be fun.<br /><br />The opening song, \\"Starlings,\\" provided me with my first impression of this CD.  Lead singer Guy Garvey uses plaintive vocals to describe the irony of being deeply in love with someone while denying that love and all the reasons that someone should find someone else.  If there is any question as to how the singer feels, it is with the closing lines:<br /><br />The violets explode inside me when I meet your eyes.<br />Then I'm spinning and I'm diving like a cloud of starlings.<br /><br />Darling is this love?<br /><br />Elbow flavors this song with several unusual features.  Raucous horns startle you against the quiet background; like maneuvering starlings, perhaps?  The drums have an African flavor.  Another instrument I do not recognize might be a glockenspiel, xylophone or carillon, but might be a synthesizer.  The combination of sounds and the soulful background vocals are clever and interesting and demands hearing again to fully appreciate.<br /><br />The song \\"The Bones of You\\" deals with separation and regret.  This time glorious guitars frequently dominate.  I also had to change my impression of this CD because I discovered that all the other songs on this CD were relatively unlike the first.  The pace of this song is much faster and the sound louder than the first song.  Singer Guy Garvey's melancholy tone is perfect for this song.<br /><br />Back to the beginnings of love is the song \\"Mirrorball.\\"  This heavily orchestrated song is a gorgeous symphony of being lost in the moment when you discover you have found your love.  Every syllable sung by Guy Garvey is fully into the feeling of the song and it is nearly impossible to avoid falling into the emotion of the moment.<br /><br />Then comes \\"Grounds for Divorce,\\" a marvelous blues song that has vague reminiscences of Tennessee Ernie Ford.  This grinder provides the title of the CD and is catchy, even though the song itself deals with a tragic subject.<br /><br />In a mellower vein is \\"An Audience with the Pope.\\"  This marvelous song about obsession reminds me a bit of 10CC.  There are lots of interesting instruments, mellow backing vocals and catchy lyrics.  Wait until the too-short guitar-dominated bridge and you will be wishing for more.<br /><br />Frankly, I am not sure what \\"Weather to Fly\\" is about.  On the other hand, the music is so mellow and mesmerizing that perhaps it makes little difference what the song means.  The horns are great.  I could have done without the vocals while the horns were playing, but that is a relatively small complaint.<br /><br />One of my favorite songs is \\"The Loneliness of a Tower Crane Driver.\\"  The bass and percussion are so marvelous that I felt more than I understood.  The bridge contains an acoustic guitar and violin or synthesizer bridge portion that is intriguing and fascinating.  This song is one that begs for loudness during the last half.<br /><br />The tempo changes substantially with a ditty called \\"The Fix.\\"  Rarely do groups sing about fixing a horse race, but here it is.  This song is another that reminds me of 10CC.<br /><br />Back in a melancholy vein is the bluesy \\"Some Riot.\\"  The subject appears to be loneliness and possibly alcoholism.  I love the keyboard work on this song, both the piano and the synthesizer.  The vocals during the final portion of this song are great and really make this song a standout on this CD.<br /><br />Elbow seems to love songs that build, and \\"One Day like This\\" builds and builds.  This love song still has a vague melancholy thread, but it is all about being lost in love.  There are moments in this song that have a Beatle's flavor, and it is all good.<br /><br />Closing out this CD is a \\"goodbye\\" song, \\"Friend of Ours.\\"  Most of this song is actually a mellow instrumental that is a very nice coda to this CD.  I always think that songs like these end up making you want to play the CD again, which makes this particular song a double goodbye song since the topic is goodbyes and it is a goodbye to the album.<br /><br />I have read a number of comments that compare Elbow with Coldplay.  I have heard several Coldplay CDs and I enjoy Coldplay, but I think Elbow is more eclectic and creative than Coldplay.  As some reviewers have said, Elbow is what Coldplay could be if they challenged themselves more.<br /><br />Sadly, radio has not been friendly to Elbow in the United States; so much good music and so little exposure.  If you enjoy 10CC, some of Elbow's music on this CD may appeal to you.  If you enjoy mellow music on an eclectic array of subjects with an interesting variety of instruments, then this music could be for you.  I know this one CD has made me a fan and I want more.<br /><br />Enjoy!is a very nice coda to this CD.  I always think that songs like these end up making you want to play the CD again, which makes this particular song a double goodbye song since the topic is goodbyes and it is a goodbye to the album. 0385512058|3.0|Keith Ferrazzi is a master networker and he believes that you can be too.  Ferrazzi, a graduate of Harvard Business School and former chief marketing officer for Deloitte Consulting and Starwood Hotels & Resorts, discovered early in his career that highly successful people have huge networks.  Who you know is often just as important as what you know.    The first key to networking is to \\"find ways to make other people more successful.\\"  Even in today's cutthroat world of business, generosity is important.  You should also stop keeping score.    You can't amass a network of connections without introducing such connections to others with equal fervor.  The more people you help, the more help you'll have and the more help you'll have helping others.  It's like the Internet.  The more people who have access, and use it, the more valuable the Internet becomes.                Never Eat Alone is filled with refreshing new approaches to relationship building.  Ferrazzi stresses that it's important to reach out to those in your circle of contacts often - not just when you need something.  He suggests meeting with others over breakfast, lunch and dinner.  Never eat alone.  \\"Invisibility is a fate far worse than failure,\\" he writes.                Ferrazzi explains the reason to build a strong web of relationships this way:    The more connections you establish, the more opportunities you'll have to make even more new connections.  As Robert Metcalfe, the inventor of Ethernet, says:  The value of a network grows proportional to the square of the number of its users.  In the case of the Internet, every new computer, every new server, and every new user added expands the possibilities for everyone else who's already there.  The same principle holds true in growing your web of relationships.  The bigger it gets, the more attractive it becomes, and the faster it grows.  That's why I say that a network is like a muscle - the more you work it, the bigger it gets.In a section called Connecting With Connectors, Ferrazzi notes that for him, certain folks provide links \\"to an entire world of people, ideas, and information that, in a very limited way, has made my own life a little more fun, helped my career along, or made the business I worked for more successful.\\"  Connectors he suggests you cultivate include restaurateurs, headhunters, lobbyists, fundraisers, public relations people, politicians and journalists.    Success isn't based on cool technology or rugged individualism, but on whom you know and how you work with them.  Increase your bottom line by helping friends connect with other friends.  Say goodbye to that dog-eat-dog world and hello to an interdependent world where we need each other more than ever.

The book consists of chapters written from the different points of view of many intersecting characters, linked in one way or another to the punk music business; and the chapters skip around in time. It requires some page-flipping to remind yourself who is who, but it's rewarding work: there is a perfect web of people and themes which come together if you stay alert.    Egan has said her subject is time, which is the goon of the title; and indeed, the passage of time/intersection of people in real life feels very much like the way this book depicts it. Connections are made and broken, then remade; people are lost and found. Broken souls sometimes mend, after a fashion, and high-flying souls are brought low, but not always all the way down. Time is a goon, and it spares no one.    There is so much to praise about this author: her incandescent language, her dialogue that sounds so real, even when spoken by people you might not normally overhear; her tone that is funny and alarming and deadpan by turns. Characters in the book meet with longing and tragedy and no scarcity of awkward moments, but the story just clips briskly along, and you are treated to dazzling images and lucid portraits. Here is Uncle Ted observing his runaway niece Sasha: \\"Her face was fragile and mischievous, pale enough to absorb hues from the world around her--purple, green, pink--like a face painted by Lucien Freud.\\"    And although the book is highly stylized--all those points of view including demented ones, one chapter delivered as a Powerpoint presentation--the style fits the story to perfection. Lives are fractured, people are wayward, time plays tricks on us.    You marvel at the depth of Egan's grasp of the personalities and language of the pop music world--what a treat to go so far inside it and still be a spectator--and the dazzling way she turns it into a metaphor for the elation and danger and fracturedness of life itself.

0913866156|5.0|I highly recommend this deck!  There is no question in my mind that it deserves 5 stars.  However, they were designed with a certain philosophy in mind, as well as a certain purpose.  The deck is very MALE...not masculine...but MALE!  This deck tends to resonate with men disproportionately and serves to awaken and stir deep feelings of masculinity and maleness in the men who use it.  I know plenty of women who also love this deck, however...especially those who are Crowley fans.  The cards are usually used less for divination and more for meditation or education on principles of Western Esotericism as understood by Crowley.  Having integrated so much symbolism into each card (color, numerology, astrology, alchemy, theology, mythology, Kabbalah, Rosicrucianism, Theosophy, Golden Dawn philosophy, Thelema, Hinduism, Egyptian wisdom, Enochian magick, etc.) the cards become more than the sum of their parts, and even mystics, such as my self, with beliefs that are quite divergent from Crowley's can learn much about themselves and the world through the potential lessons contained therein.  The cards are larger than most, and the imagery is more vivid.  The cards were actually designed to evoke certain states in the user...be prepared for an emotional response to the cards.  This deck is also historically and culturally significant as it is probably the second most widely used deck, and more influential than the Rider-Waite deck because it carries a (sometimes pedantic) philosophy with it that informed much of Western culture after World War II (though indirectly).  Your favorite politician's favorite rock star's favorite author's favorite intellectual was probably influenced by this deck and its creator, whether you realize it or not.  Through use of this deck, you are tapping into a stream of culture that is not necessarily right or wrong, but significant and relevant at the very least.    I would recommend buying this deck in conjunction with a book that explains some ofCrowley's (highly misunderstood) ideas.  Anything by Lon Milo DuQuette is a good start.  He does a good job of sifting through Crowley's irreverent and inflammatory cries for attention to get at the essence of his more sincere ideas.

B00005LANG|5.0|EXODUS is an album that completely defines not only an artist/band but the generation in which it/they grew up in, the album was recorded and subsequently released.  Bob Marley and The Wailers were truly a pop, mainstream phenomena unlike any other by the time this wonderful album was released in 1977 as has been stated and documented countless times.  The world was not only fascinated by the Rastafarian beliefs but the revolutionary principals of Reggae.  The 1960's & 1970's were truly times of revolution on a worldwide scale & NO band or group of artists signified this better than The Wailers.<br /><br />Time Magazine voted this album as the most important of the 20th century and for good reason, Bob Marley and The Wailers in both of it's incarnations during the 1960's and 1970's brought forth such powerful messages and themes that would do more than redefine music, which it did, but would also become, in many ways, the voice of revolutions on just about every continent under the sun.  Reggae or \\"Island Music\\", as it was commonly referred, was more than a genre, it was a belief and lifestyle.  The Wailers did for Island Music what Chuck Berry had done for Rock & Roll some 20 years earlier, they become a polarizing and solidifying force of a genre.<br /><br />This album was unparelled in it's effect on social consciousness and it's far reaching implications both musically and socially.  No other album had the type of worldwide effect that this one did period, thus the awarding of it's number one position by Time Magazine.  The Wailers and in particular Bob Marley became one of the most beloved and respected artists in music history for being not only great songwriters and performers but true poets and revolutionaries in every since of that word.<br /><br />EXODUS is Marley's crowning achievement, now I know many will point to some of his earlier material with the original Wailers line up including the grear Peter Tosh and Bunny Wailer as better music and I agree that those recordings were splendid and set the foundation for both the band as a whole and all 3 individually and would be used as a platform for their future musically expressions.  However, the greatness of this album cannot be overstated nor underestimated and I believe this line up doesn't get the full credit they deserve for the material they produced.  Bob was the leader, songwriter and visionary but it takes a talented group of individuals to relay his message to the masses with the grace that they were able to pull off.<br /><br />This album shows Marley's incredible versatility as a songwriter, you have it all on full display, revolution, mystical themes based upon Rastafarian beliefs, songs of love and passion, songs of hope and happiness.  I believe this album is best listened to all the way through as it has a natural flow that truly comes through with a full listen.  The epic title track is one of the most incredible display's of musicianship ever recorded and was an out of this world experience live.<br /><br />The influence of this album, artist and band on a worldwide scale has been achieved by very few artists in the history of music and this is the greatest example of what made Bob Marley an artist for all seasons, times and ages.  This is must listening for anyone who truly wants to grasp how music can change perceptions and beliefs on a worldwide scale.  Time Magazine got it right on this album and when you consider all of the other monumental albums to be released in the 20th century, it shows just how much Bob Marley, The Wailers and their music meant to listeners as a whole.at those recordings were splendid and set the foundation for both the band as a whole and all 3 individually and would be used as a platform for their future musically expressions. 116932701X|4.0|***SPOILER ALERT***<br /><br />D. H. Lawrence published Lady Chatterley's Lover in 1928, two years before he died, however the novel wouldn't appear in its unexpurgated form until 1960. The story centres on Lady Constance Chatterley and her affairs with two men. Although the title focusses on the singular lover, Lady Chatterley does engage in two extramarital affairs. Lady Chatterley is married to Sir Clifford, who was paralyzed in World War I and left impotent. The Chatterleys are childless and Sir Clifford gives his wife approval to have a whirlwind affair for the sole purpose of getting herself pregnant to produce an heir to his estate and fortune. I am sure the British censors had reasons to disapprove of the novel on this basis alone, before any sex is depicted at all. Permitting members of the aristrocracy to fool around under the full knowledge of both married parties (early twentieth-century \\"swinging\\") was taboo, regardless who was doing it. Lady Chatterley's Lover also caused so much controversy because it crossed British social classes with Lady Constance's long affair with Oliver Mellors, the estate's pheasant-tending gamekeeper.<br /><br />The language used in the novel is another issue in itself, as Lawrence writes unflinchingly with swear words and depicts various sex acts and sex play. In 1928 England, such writing was considered obscene. I myself was surprised that the foulest language of 1920's England would be so close to what is still said today. The lover in the title, Mellors, feels most at ease when he speaks in his Derby dialect, and Lawrence approximates his speech within the confines of modern typeface with plenty of apostrophes and elisions. It was not difficult to read, and easy to figure out if I read the dialect aloud. Mellors often shifts from dialect to proper and formal English, and often confounds the upper classes by being able to speak to them like a perfect gentleman. Mellors speaks like a college-age drunken sailor when engaging in sex or sex play with Lady Chatterley, and Lawrence's Harlequin Romance euphemisms seem beautiful, and not trite, in their imagery.<br /><br />Over the course of my reading of Lawrence's novels, I have noticed his tendency to write one observation then immediately afterward contradict that point or write its opposite. This is encountered throughout Lady Chatterley's Lover. While Constance sits in on a meeting her husband has with some gentleman friends:<br /><br />\\"She liked to hear what they had to say, especially when Tommy was there. It was fun. Instead of men kissing you, and touching you with their bodies, they revealed their minds to you. It was great fun! But what cold minds!<br />\\"And also it was a little irritating.\\"<br /><br />Clifford, paralyzed and in a wheelchair after the Great War and seeking to find new ways to occupy his time, aspires to fame and fortune by being a successful writer. As he embarks on his literary career:<br /><br />\\"Clifford, of course, had still many childish taboos and fetishes. He wanted to be thought 'really good,' which was all cock-a-hoopy nonsense. What was really good was what actually caught on. It was no good being really good and getting left with it. It seemed as if most of the 'really good' men just missed the bus. After all you only lived one life, and if you missed the bus, you were just left on the pavement, along with the rest of the failures.\\"<br /><br />I wonder if Lawrence projected his own literary aspirations onto Clifford. Lawrence probably felt the pull of mass popularity with mediocre work versus obscurity with well-reviewed, yet unsold, work. I found it amusing that he used William James's term for success, the \\"bitch goddess\\", throughout the novel, in Clifford's quest for fame.<br /><br />Lady Chatterley discovers that she is pregnant by Mellors, and while Sir Clifford did give his consent for her to go out and have a fling for the sole purpose of conceiving, he expressly forbade her to carry on a relationship with whatever man who fathered her child. Lady Chatterley and Mellors decide to divorce their spouses and move away, perhaps to British Columbia (I love the Canadian connection) and when Constance tells her husband of her plans, he is left stupefied, immobile, unable to talk and virtually paralyzed across his entire body when he discovers that the man his wife had been carrying on with was his own servant. The final chapters are filled with tension, drama and suspense. I could not put the book down as Lady Chatterley and Mellors devised ways to save their reputations, try to live discreetly and to counter their critics. The tangled web they wove was a rapid page-turner, and made me sad that the novel was not two hundred pages longer like Sons and Lovers or Women in Love.y Chatterley and Mellors decide to divorce their spouses and move away, perhaps to British Columbia (I love the Canadian connection) and when Constance tells her husband of her plans, he is left stupefied, immobile, unable to talk and virtually paralyzed across his entire body when he discovers that the man his wife had been carrying on with was his own servant. B0002KZAKS|5.0|Price and performance wise, this mic is as good or better than the sm58.      I have been using 3 the of Behringer xm8500 mics in my home studio for over 5 years now.  The sound or 'flavor' of this mic is almost identical to an early 90's Shure sm58 that I also use in the studio.  The only noticeable difference between the two (sound wise) is the xm8500 has a tiny bit more output, and the presence peak is slightly lower in the frequency scale - I would describe this as the sm58 peak being slightly airy and cutting, and the xm8500 being thick and meaty.  If you are using this mic with a 3 band eq, you can bump the mids slightly and match the sound of the xm8500 to that of the sm58 with no problem.    Build wise, this mic is as beastly and tank-like as the sm58.  It has a nice heft to it, solid metal housing, all that good stuff.      This mic excels on vocals, close mic'ing drums, bass cabs, guitar cabs,...basically anywhere you would normally use an sm58, you can use this mic there and it will perform like a champ.  My favorite task for this mic is bass amps, and toms.  The presence bump on this mic makes toms sit just right in the mix w/out having to fuss with the eq too much (you get the nice low end 'thwump' and the necessary mid range 'slap' to not only hear, but FEEL the toms in the mix).    Do yourself a favor and build some xlr patch cables with resistor(s) in them to better match the low impedance signal of this dynamic mic to the high impedance inputs of today's mic preamps.  You will find that the mic will perform as it (or actually the sm58 it is modeled after) was designed to.  Google 'taming the shure' for more info.    For about $20, this mic definitely beats out the sm58 in my book.  Don't be a gear snob,...get your money's worth and try out this mic.

Perhaps the Coverdale period is my favorite because an album like Come Taste the Band appeals to me with its funky rhythms and soulful vocal melodies, but the very first lineup offers instant satisfaction as well.      Yes, these songs sound horribly dated.  The year is 1968 so it's understandable.  Yes the majority of the album is loaded with cover songs, however this is an *extremely* rare exception where a band actually goes the extra distance to make the cover songs different, and arguably better (though whether these cover songs are actually better or not is completely up to the listener).    We all know the wonderful verse melody and chorus from \\"Hush\\" because radio stations have been doing a number on that song for years, and you know, despite being overplayed, I still love it.  In fact I always turn it up when I hear it on the radio.  The truth is, the song always reminded me of Steam's \\"Na Na Hey Hey Kiss Him Goodbye\\" and as a child I'd get the two songs confused, however nowadays I prefer the Deep Purple song because the Steam track has been murdered by overexposure whether it be audience participation in WWE events bringing the song to peoples attention, or the classic rock FM radio station format itself.    I'm also a big fan of the vocal melody in \\"One More Rainy Day\\".  The lead singer is seriously *almost* as good as Ian Gillan on this particular track.    Now some of these cover songs are a bit overlong, but on the other hand there's a reason for it- they add a lot.  The prelude to \\"Prelude: Happiness/I'm So Glad\\" is REALLY cool, and the same can be said for the intro to \\"Hey Joe\\".  The organ is a fantastic musical instrument, and the way the organ is used in these two songs gives a distinct feeling of a mysterious and dark place.      I gotta admit that the chorus repeats WAY too much during the \\"I'm So Glad\\" part, and I believe it was the same way in the original version as well.  Too bad- had it been trimmed by a couple minutes I wouldn't be complaining about it at all.  As for the vocals in \\"Hey Joe\\", well they aren't *quite* as compassionately delivered as in the famous Hendrix version, but they're hardly a disappointment either.  Perhaps the entire song is performed slightly slower than the Hendrix version.      This version of \\"Help\\" is absolutely INCREDIBLE!  It's a *drastically* slower-paced version of the Beatles song which actually makes it sound significantly more personal and emotional.  I don't know guys, I love the Beatles and everything, but this version might be more appealing to me.  Perhaps I'm just blown away by how different it sounds and I need time to figure out which version I prefer.     Other songs like \\"Mandrake Root\\" contain incredibly sad vocals before eventually turning into a pretty spectacular guitar jam, and \\"Love Help Me\\" is just a beautifully written song.      Overall the early version of Deep Purple isn't nearly as forgettable as some might believe.  I highly recommend this and the Book of Taliesyn albums as a part of your rock library.

Oh, and Cuddles the kitten.<br /><br />Sara starts to become suspicious of Rebecca's behaviour after she meets Rebecca's parents who are concerned about and frightened by Rebecca. More people get hurt and eventually, Sara and Rebecca confront.<br /><br />So the plot is good. The suspense is also good. Yes the film is predictable but it is not too gory, certainly not the least bit difficult to understand, and makes sense for the most part. The acting of the two lead characters, Sara and Rebecca, is also quite good and believable.<br /><br />The bad: the film seems to rush along faster than it makes sense. A little bit more lead in to the roommate's obsession with Sara would be more believable. The other characters are boring and stereotyped; the boyfriend spends most of his time squinting and trying to look cool, the friends Irene and Tracy seem to have nothing to their characters. I liked Billy Zane and would have liked to see a bigger part for him. Even the part where Tracy seduces him to damage his reputation is not believable because the film rushes through that. The portrayal of college life was also completely stereotypical.<br /><br />I agree with another reviewer's statements: If you're looking to kill some time with a fun movie..this is for you! If you are looking for something with substance, depth, originality, plot, and a storyline that keeps you enthralled to the bitter end...keep it moving this isn't your cup of tea!<br /><br />I was just looking to kill time with an ok movie so it achieved that purpose.
